        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }

          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Summary

:

<strong><!---->Summary:</strong>


          


          

Debug check failed: !has_optimized_code


          

(was: Security: Debug check failed: !has_optimized_code)


          

<br>


        




          



Labels

:

<strong><!---->Labels:</strong>


          


          

-Restrict-View-SecurityTeam -Security_Severity-High -Security_Impact-Beta Type-Bug


          




          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Summary:</strong>
          
          Debug check failed: !has_optimized_code
          (was: Security: Debug check failed: !has_optimized_code)
          <br>
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Labels:</strong>
          
          -Restrict-View-SecurityTeam -Security_Severity-High -Security_Impact-Beta Type-Bug
          
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









This is an edge case where we:



<span class="line"><!---->This is an edge case where we:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  1. Start compiling a function with Maglev, state is marked "in progress"



<span class="line"><!---->  1. Start compiling a function with Maglev, state is marked "in progress"<!----></span>



<br>





  2. Another closure of that function is created, --always-turbofan clobbers the state with "request TF"



<span class="line"><!---->  2. Another closure of that function is created, --always-turbofan clobbers the state with "request TF"<!----></span>



<br>





  3. The TF code compiles, then immediately deopts, resetting the tiering state to none.



<span class="line"><!---->  3. The TF code compiles, then immediately deopts, resetting the tiering state to none.<!----></span>



<br>





  4. That second closure starts another Maglev compilation.



<span class="line"><!---->  4. That second closure starts another Maglev compilation.<!----></span>



<br>





  5. The first Maglev compilation finally finishes, setting the feedback vector slot.



<span class="line"><!---->  5. The first Maglev compilation finally finishes, setting the feedback vector slot.<!----></span>



<br>





  6. The second Maglev compilation finishes, hitting this DCHECK.



<span class="line"><!---->  6. The second Maglev compilation finishes, hitting this DCHECK.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since this only happens because --always-turbofan forces a synchronous compilation and clobbers tiering state, I'm tempted to fix this by making --always-turbofan imply --no-maglev. Either way, not a security issue.



<span class="line"><!---->Since this only happens because --always-turbofan forces a synchronous compilation and clobbers tiering state, I'm tempted to fix this by making --always-turbofan imply --no-maglev. Either way, not a security issue.<!----></span>
